# Widened Grammar Diagnostic

- Deterministic enumerative beam search with beam `50`, steps `10`, `keep_all_until_step=2`, seeds `{x, 1}`, and no continuous coefficient fitting.
- Added unary operators: `sin`, `cos`, `tan`, `sinh`, `cosh`, `tanh`, `erf`, `gamma`, `J0`.
- Residual modes: `zm_residual` and `post_is_residual = log(f) - ZM - ((x-1)-log(x))`.

## Complete Works of Shakespeare / zm_residual

- single-ZM `c`: `244.844847773631`

## Pride and Prejudice / zm_residual

- single-ZM `c`: `34.119420842756`
- original step-2 winner: `eml[sub[x,1],eml[x,1]]`
- original step-2 math: `EML((x-1),EML(x,1))`
- widened step-2 winner: `sub[erf[x],sin[x]]`
- widened step-2 math: `(erf(x)-sin(x))`
- widened step-2 matches original: `False`
- widened step-2 is prior Bregman winner: `False`
- any widened winner uses new operator: `True`
- any widened top-10 uses new operator: `True`

## Pride and Prejudice / post_is_residual

- single-ZM `c`: `34.119420842756`
- original step-2 winner: `eml[sub[x,1],eml[x,1]]`
- original step-2 math: `EML((x-1),EML(x,1))`
- widened step-2 winner: `mul[sub[x,1],sub[1,x]]`
- widened step-2 math: `((x-1)*(1-x))`
- widened step-2 matches original: `False`
- widened step-2 is prior Bregman winner: `False`
- any widened winner uses new operator: `True`
- any widened top-10 uses new operator: `True`
